For the lack of a high-speed pMOS device, it is hard to design the inverter for pulse amplification, so we have replaced it with the broadband amplifier using the device GALI 84+ InGaP HBT from Mini-Circuits, Brooklyn, NY, to verify the concept of the proposed architecture. A Sirenza SHF-0289 MESFET is used to implement the PAs. The designed class-D and class-F PAs have 51.7% and 69% continuous wave (CW) PAE at 29 and 27 dBm, respectively. It is valuable to compare the power consumption of the digital baseband processor and PA. The dc power consumption of the FPGA is relatively small compared to that of the PA, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig15" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 15</a>, thus the effect on the overall efficiency is not significant.</p><p>The efficiency and output power degrade from the above value due to the on resistance of the switch device on the drain node. Moreover, due to the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta\Sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-88-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-88">\Delta\Sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula> switching effect, the output power is also degraded. Since the average duty ratio of the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta\Sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-89-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-89">\Delta\Sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-digitized CDMA IS-95A envelope signal is approximately 50%, one-half of the full current of the device flows under the switching operation so that the output power is reduced by 3 dB.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig16" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 16</a> shows the time-domain output signal of the class-D amplifier. Since the response time of the designed class-D amplifier for the pulse is 10 ns, it shows the limitation in following the pulse stream when the width of minimum pulse period is less than 20 ns, according to <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn15" href="#deqn15" class="fulltext-link">(15)</a>. As a result, it is hard for the PA to exactly respond to the pulse stream as the sample rate increases more than 50 MHz. Compared to the class-D PA, the class-F PA has the reduced device capacitance, which allows the higher sample rate. The rising and falling times decrease to nearly half so that it can follow the pulse stream up to 100 MHz. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig17" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 17</a> shows the time-domain output signal of the class-F PA. The detailed view of the time-domain output signals are presented in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig18" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 18</a>. They explain the decrease of the output power and efficiency caused by the imperfect switching (slew effect depending on <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{\rm ds}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-90-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-90">C_{\rm ds}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) at the high sample rate. The variation in the pulsewidth is not so significant that the linearity degradation by slewing is not serious.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig16"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4387657/4381295/4381295-fig-16-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4387657/4381295/4381295-fig-16-small.gif" alt="Figure 16" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 16. </b><fig><p>Time-domain output signal of the class-D PA at: (a) <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\ {\hbox{sample rate}} =20-{\hbox {MHz}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-91-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-91">\ {\hbox{sample rate}} =20-{\hbox {MHz}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and (b) <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\hbox{sample rate}} =80-{\hbox {MHz}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-92-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-92">{\hbox{sample rate}} =80-{\hbox {MHz}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4381295/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig17"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4387657/4381295/4381295-fig-17-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4387657/4381295/4381295-fig-17-small.gif" alt="Figure 17" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 17. </b><fig><p>Time-domain output signal of the class-F PA at: (a) <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\ {\hbox{sample rate}} =20-{\hbox {MHz}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-93-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-93">\ {\hbox{sample rate}} =20-{\hbox {MHz}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and (b) <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\hbox{sample rate}} =80-{\hbox {MHz}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-94-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-94">{\hbox{sample rate}} =80-{\hbox {MHz}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4381295/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig18"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4387657/4381295/4381295-fig-18-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4387657/4381295/4381295-fig-18-small.gif" alt="Figure 18" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 18. </b><fig><p>Measured time-domain output signals of: (a) the class-D amplifier and (b) the class-F amplifier at 80-MHz sample rate: The degradation of the output power and efficiency comes from the limited slew rate of the PA. The pulsewidth does not significantly change.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4381295/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full table" id="table1"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table I </b>DC Bias and <span class="MathJax_Preview">P{\rm in}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-95-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-95">P{\rm in}</script> Conditions of Class-D PA at <span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm OSR}=32</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-96-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-96">{\rm OSR}=32</script><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4387657/4381295/4381295-table-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4387657/4381295/4381295-table-1-small.gif" alt="Table I" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<div class="figure figure-full table" id="table2"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table II </b>DC Bias and <span class="MathJax_Preview">P{\rm in}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-97-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-97">P{\rm in}</script> Conditions of Class-F PA at <span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm OSR}=32</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-98-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-98">{\rm OSR}=32</script><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4387657/4381295/4381295-table-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4387657/4381295/4381295-table-2-small.gif" alt="Table II" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<p></p><p>The maximum efficiency of the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta\Sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-99-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-99">\Delta\Sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-digitized transmitter is obtained by optimizing the input power with the proper dc-bias voltage, whose control is conducted by the FPGA. The dc-bias conditions with appropriate input powers for various average output power levels are presented in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Tables I</a> and <a ref-type="table" anchor="table2" class="fulltext-link">II</a>, and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig19" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 19</a> shows the efficiency versus output power. For the average output power range of 10.8–22.1 dBm, the measured power-added efficiency (PAE) of the class-F PA are 48.6%–51.7%. The <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta_{\rm overall}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-100-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-100">\eta_{\rm overall}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta\Sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-101-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-101">\Delta\Sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-digitized PA calculated using the value obtained in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2b" class="fulltext-link">Section II-B</a> is 31%, which can be improved using the better amplifier. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig19" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 19</a> also shows that the class-F PA has a relatively low drop in PAE versus sampling frequency than the class-D PA.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig19"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4387657/4381295/4381295-fig-19-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4387657/4381295/4381295-fig-19-small.gif" alt="Figure 19" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 19. </b><fig><p>Measured efficiency of class-D and class-F PAs with the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta\Sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-102-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-102">\Delta\Sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-digitized envelope signal for CDMA IS-95A signal. The sampling frequency varies from 20 to 80 MHz. For the class-D PA, the efficiency suddenly drops as the sampling frequency is higher than 50 MHz. (The efficiency of the dc/dc converter is not considered here.)</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4381295/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig20"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4387657/4381295/4381295-fig-20-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4387657/4381295/4381295-fig-20-small.gif" alt="Figure 20" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 20. </b><fig><p>Measured output spectra of 1-bit <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta\Sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-103-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-103">\Delta\Sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-digitized transmitter with various OSRs. They show good match with the simulation results.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4381295/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>As mentioned above, the 80-MHz <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">({\rm OSR}=32)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-104-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-104">({\rm OSR}=32)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> sample rate satisfies the minimum linearity requirements for the CDMA IS-95A signal. The lower sample rate (lower OSR) of the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta\Sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-105-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-105">\Delta\Sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula> modulator generates more quantization noise, as presented in <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn10" href="#deqn10" class="fulltext-link">(10)</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a>. The measured results in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig20" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 20</a> match quite well with the simulation results. It also verifies that the sample rate of 80 MHz satisfies the specification, while the sample rates of 20 and 40 MHz are not enough. At the maximal average output power, the measured adjacent channel power ratios (ACPRs) are <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-106-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-106">-</script></tex-math></inline-formula>46.6 and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-107-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-107">-</script></tex-math></inline-formula>57.9 dBc at 885-kHz and 1.98-MHz offsets, respectively. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig21" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 21</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig22" class="fulltext-link">22</a> show that the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta\Sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-108-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-108">\Delta\Sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-digitized transmitter achieves high linearity over the broad range of average output power levels.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig21"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4387657/4381295/4381295-fig-21-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4387657/4381295/4381295-fig-21-small.gif" alt="Figure 21" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 21. </b><fig><p>Measured ACPRs of class-D and class-F PAs with 80-MHz <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta\Sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-109-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-109">\Delta\Sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-digitized envelope signal for CDMA IS-95A signal.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4381295/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig22"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4387657/4381295/4381295-fig-22-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4387657/4381295/4381295-fig-22-small.gif" alt="Figure 22" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 22. </b><fig><p>Power spectrum densities of the output signal at 12 and 22 dBm.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4381295/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig23"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4387657/4381295/4381295-fig-23-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4387657/4381295/4381295-fig-23-small.gif" alt="Figure 23" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 23. </b><fig><p><inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta\Sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-110-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-110">\Delta\Sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-digitized transmitter employing three-level quantizer.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4381295/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The out-of-band noise is the critical issue in this transmitter. For the 80-MHz sample rate, the implemented transmitter requires an additional bandpass filter to reduce the noise in the Rx band. If the sample rate can be increased higher than 250 MHz, with the help of a duplexer positioned behind the PA, the fourth-order <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta\Sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-111-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-111">\Delta\Sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-modulator enables the transmitter without the additional bandpass filter, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7(b)</a>. Another possible method is to utilize the sinc filtering mechanism occurred in the discrete to analog conversion process. For 20- and 40-MHz sample rates, the zero of the sinc filter is located at the Rx band so that the out-of-band noise reduces. In that case, however, the noise in the Tx band is not low enough that the multibit approach is required.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Multibit Approach</h2></div><p>The multibit quantizer reduces the amount of the quantization noise at the overall band. This means the enhancement of the efficiency and linearity. As the number of quantization bits increases, however, it gets harder to control the PA. Moreover, to amplify the envelope signal efficiently, 1-bit characteristic is preferred. It can be done by using the cell array of the unit PAs. Each unit PA is turned on and off according to the control signal. This is a conceptually good candidate for the multibit PA, but there is a problem in combining the power signals from the multiple PA cells, which can be solved using the uneven power-combining concept of the Doherty amplifier <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref25" id="context_ref_25_5">[25]</a>.</p><p>To remove the power-combining loss, we utilize just one PA while the multibit information is delivered through the multiple power supply array. They consist of switches and multiple voltage sources having different dc voltages. The array of switches are orthogonally turned on, thus there is no power-combining problem in this structure. To verify the concept of the multibit PA, the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta\Sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-112-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-112">\Delta\Sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula> modulator employing a three-level quantizer is designed. The output signal from the three-level quantizer is encoded to two-way 1-bit signals in the FPGA and delivered to the switch in the same way as described in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4" class="fulltext-link">Section IV</a>. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig23" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 23</a> describes how the three-level digitized PA works. The three-level system is implemented with the 40-MHz sample rate due to the speed limitation of the FPGA. The experimental results in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig24" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 24</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig25" class="fulltext-link">25</a> show that the output signal of the PA has a three-level digitized envelope with reduced quantization noise. It also reduces the Rx band noise quite well with one zero by sinc filtering, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig26" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 26</a>. The modulation efficiency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta_{\rm mod}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-113-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-113">\eta_{\rm mod}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta\Sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-114-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-114">\Delta\Sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula> modulator is improved to 89% and the PAE of the PA is 54.6% at 20 dBm of the average output power with the CDMA IS-95A signal. The consequent overall efficiency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta_{\rm overall}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-115-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-115">\eta_{\rm overall}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is 48.6%, which is already very good.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig24"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4387657/4381295/4381295-fig-24-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4387657/4381295/4381295-fig-24-small.gif" alt="Figure 24" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 24. </b><fig><p>Time-domain output signal of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta\Sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-116-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-116">\Delta\Sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-digitized transmitter employing three-level quantizer.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4381295/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig25"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4387657/4381295/4381295-fig-25-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4387657/4381295/4381295-fig-25-small.gif" alt="Figure 25" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 25. </b><fig><p>Output spectra of 40-MHz second-order <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta\Sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-117-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-117">\Delta\Sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula> digitized transmitter employing two-level (1 bit) and three-level quantizers with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm OSR}=16</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-118-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-118">{\rm OSR}=16</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (40 MHz).</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4381295/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig26"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4387657/4381295/4381295-fig-26-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4387657/4381295/4381295-fig-26-small.gif" alt="Figure 26" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 26. </b><fig><p>Measured Tx and Rx band spectra for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta\Sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-119-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-119">\Delta\Sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-modulator employing three-level quantizer. The zero induced by sinc filtering lowers the amount of the quantization noise at Rx band, but the mismatch by the “dirty”clock deteriorates the filtering effect.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4381295/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec6"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION VI.</div><h2>Conclusions</h2></div><p>The RF transmitter employing the constant envelope modulator has been designed and implemented. Among the various modulators, the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta\Sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-120-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-120">\Delta\Sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula> modulator has been chosen for its noise-shaping characteristic. The linearity and efficiency of the transmitter highly depends on the quantization noise, and the appropriate quantization level and OSR have been determined to reduce the quantization noise. The 80-MHz <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta\Sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-121-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-121">\Delta\Sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula> modulator with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">1/0</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-122-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-122">1/0</script></tex-math></inline-formula> quantization satisfies the minimum linearity specification of the CDMA IS-95A signal. To realize the circuit, we have heavily utilized the digital environment (FPGA) and combined the modulated envelope signal with the up-converted phase signal through the PA. The class-D and class-F PAs have been fabricated and compared for the optimum operation with the digitized envelope. The measurement results have verified that the most important factor in the digitized operation of the PA is to alleviate the slewing effect by the device capacitances, and the amplifier with small device capacitance is suitable for this application. For the experiment using the CDMA IS-95A signal, the measured overall efficiency is 31% at 22.1-dBm average output power, while the linearity requirements have been satisfied. This transmitter has provided high efficiency and linearity over all usable output power levels. The noise power at the receiver band can be suppressed successfully by introducing zeros in the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta\Sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-123-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-123">\Delta\Sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula> modulator and with the help of the duplexer. To enhance the performance further, a multibit quantizer has been employed with a new combining method. It eliminates the efficiency degradation from the power-combining loss by using the multiple switch array. The implemented 40-MHz three-level <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta\Sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-124-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-124">\Delta\Sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-digitized RF transmitter has presented 48.6% of the overall efficiency at 20-dBm average output power. The performance can be further enhanced by developing the higher multibit digital PA with better efficiency. For the full utilization of the transmitter architecture, we should solve the switching speed limitation of the PA and the out-of-band noise problem in the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta\Sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-125-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-125">\Delta\Sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula> modulator, hopefully without employing the output filter. However, this architecture can be easily applied to the modulator application as it is.</p></div>
<h3>ACKNOWLEDGMENT</h3><p>The authors would like to thank Prof. A. Khandani and S. Chaudhuri, both with the University of Waterloo, Waterloo, ON, Canada, for their great support. The authors also thank to J. Moon, Pohang University of Science and Technology (POSTECH), Pohang, Gyungbuk, Korea, for his help with printed circuit board (PCB) fabrication.</p></div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

j$('document').ready(function(){
	if(getCookie('legacyUserName')!=null)

the digitized envelope signal to control the drain voltage of a switching mode power amplifier (PA). It is based on a novel polar modulation using the constant envelope modulated signal. Among the various constant envelope modulators, the DeltaSigma modulator is chosen for its noise-shaping characteristic. It enables the use of a highly efficient switching amplifier with high linearity. For demonstration, the overall transmitter is implemented and tested with a code-division multiple-access IS-95A signal. The class-D and class-F amplifiers are designed and compared for the optimum operation. The experimental results show that the amplifier with small device size is suitable for this application because of the fast switching requirement. For the class-F amplifier, the measured power-added efficiency is 51.7% at 22.1 dBm and the overall efficiency (considering the amplified quantization noise) is 31%. The adjacent channel power ratios at 885 kHz and 1.98 MHz are lower than -44.9 and -55.6 dBc at the output power range from 10.8 to 22.1 dBm without any pre-distortion techniques. The overall efficiency is improved to 48.6% with a three-level quantized DeltaSigma modulator. The results clearly show that the highly efficient switching mode PA can be controlled efficiently using a digital signal from the DeltaSigma envelope modulation technique.","doi":"10.1109/TMTT.2007.907137","startPage":"2679","publicationTitle":"IEEE Transactions on Microwave Theory and Techniques","endPage":"2690","isJournal":true,"isConference":false,"dateOfInsertion":"10 December 2007","publisher":"IEEE","accessionNumber":"9883903","htmlLink":"/document/4381295/","isEarlyAccess":false,"isBook":false,"isEphemera":false,"isOpenAccess":false,"isSMPTE":false,"journalDisplayDateOfPublication":"10 December 2007","chronOrPublicationDate":"Dec.  2007","isFreeDocument":false,"isCustomDenial":false,"persistentLink":"http://ieeexplore.ieee.org/servlet/opac?punumber=22","isStaticHtml":true,"isNotDynamicOrStatic":false,"htmlAbstractLink":"/document/4381295/","isPromo":false,"isDynamicHtml":true,"isStandard":false,"publicationDate":"Dec. 2007","conferenceDate":" ","isACM":false,"issue":"12","volume":"55","startPage":"2679","openAccessFlag":"no","ephemeraFlag":"false","title":"A &lt;formula formulatype=\"inline\"&gt;&lt;tex&gt;$\\Delta\\Sigma$&lt;/tex&gt;
